        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Just kidding. There is no such thing as a Tuffy Gosewisch. (Patrick Dubuque)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Tuffy Gosewisch is unquestionably one of the greatest baseball names in the sport today. In addition, following Miguel Montero shipping off to Chicago, Gosewisch is penciled in as the Diamondbacks' primary backstop for 2015. His only competition for the job is Rule 5 pick Oscar Hernandez -- who has never played an inning above A-ball -- and Jordan Pacheco, who isn't nearly good enough defensively to play regularly behind the plate. Gosewisch could be in line for a heavy dose of playing time this season, which is likely enough to make him relevant in NL-only and two-catcher leagues. .240 is probably the ceiling for his batting average, but if the decent pop he's displayed in the high minors (34 home runs in 367 games since 2010) translates to the majors, 10+ homers is certainly possible. (<a href="https://twitter.com/scottstrandberg">Scott Strandberg</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>There's nothing sexy about Tuffy Gosewisch as a fantasy option. However, it appears that he will be getting the lion's share of starts behind the plate in Arizona, making him worth a look in NL-only and two-catcher leagues, simply due to volume.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Diamondbacks' catching situation looked somewhat bleak after Miguel Montero was sent packing in December 2014. The combination of Gerald Laird and Gosewisch was supposed to suffice. Laird played all of one game and Gosewisch suffered a torn ACL in June that ended his 2015 season. Gosewisch, 32, isn't much with the bat -- never has been, likely never will be. He hit just .211/.261/.281 in 138 plate appearances. If fantasy baseball was scored on the strength of one's name, Gosewisch would be Bryce Harper. Alas, it is not, and Gosewisch has almost no value on the fantasy front. With Welington Castillo's emergence last season and Gosewisch's return from the injury, he might struggle to find 138 plate appearances in 2016.(Dustin Nosler)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The classic "all glove, no hit" catcher with one of the best names in baseball, Tuffy Gosewich hit a career-high in 2015 with 138 plate appearances. It follows that his 13 RBIs and nine runs scored were also career highs.Â </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
